  <span id="freeText12316884845669308451" style="display:none">Blimey. This started off quite well. Lucifer, a witty queen, given a last chance by God of redemption if he can live a good life in human form for year. Lucifer, of course, has different ideas. <br />But, gosh. I once had someone next to me in a plane turn around in their seat, look for a convenient place to vomit, and then empty the entire contents of their stomach over me and my kindle, both of us sitting peacefully together minding our own business. Reading this book was a bit like that experience except that instead of Singapore Airlines chunks and odd yellow-coloured slime, this was words. <br />No more, I cried (in both cases, actually).<br />I had to give up on this book. Most of my reading these days seems to be done in a slightly inebriated state. For many books this is a distinct improvement, but not this one. I think Satan won in the end, but I honestly didn't care.</span>

<div id="review_924102841" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/924102841" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5938821-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/924102841?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/5938821-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer924102841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15251623115494207711">This book is definitely NOT for the faint of heart or the weak of stomach. That said, if you have a dark sense of humor, this is the book for you.<br/><br/>Lucifer is the best anti-hero of all time. What makes this book so special (besides the high quality of the writing itself) is that Duncan manages to make the character both sympathetic and, well, as horrible as you would expect Lucifer to be. He commits terrible acts and says terrible things while still managing to be hilarious and likeable. The depth</span>
  <span id="freeText15251623115494207711" style="display:none">This book is definitely NOT for the faint of heart or the weak of stomach. That said, if you have a dark sense of humor, this is the book for you.<br /><br />Lucifer is the best anti-hero of all time. What makes this book so special (besides the high quality of the writing itself) is that Duncan manages to make the character both sympathetic and, well, as horrible as you would expect Lucifer to be. He commits terrible acts and says terrible things while still managing to be hilarious and likeable. The depth of this book is found in how God and the uncorrupted angels are depicted: at best morally ambiguous and at worst outright hypocritical and creepily detached from humanity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15251623115494207711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_984729327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984729327" />
    <a title="Belhor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22189980-belhor"><img alt="Belhor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518135215p2/22189980.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/984729327?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Belhor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Belhor" href="/user/show/22189980-belhor">Belhor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189980-belhor?shelf=novels">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer984729327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7142842576001065472">I really expected Lucifer to be smarter, wittier and more charming. The premise that Lucifer is in fact "Bad" was a serious put down. I wasn't expecting the writer to be loyal to the modern- let's say Christian- definition of Satan. The writing style is sometimes hard to follow, and the sentences -sometimes- hardly make any sense. But still a moderately good book. It did have a few good lines. It's a pity that such a beautiful idea was not presented in its best possible form. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2668761495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2668761495" />
    <a title="JoAnne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8346252-joanne"><img alt="JoAnne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334681224p2/8346252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2668761495?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JoAnne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JoAnne" href="/user/show/8346252-joanne">JoAnne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2668761495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1535497269231275541">I wanted to enjoy this, as I enjoyed Glen Duncan's "Last Werewolf" series. This has the same grittiness, salaciousness, and dirtiness, plus a dab of historic lore that adds some spice; but I just couldn't get into "I, Lucifer" as much.<br/><br/>Glen Duncan's writing style is hard to follow at times, and the plot seems... I don't even know. It's sorta linear, but not really. Jumping back and forth between the Biblical times and Now, a time the Devil is loaned a human body by heavens to try things out. Body</span>
  <span id="freeText1535497269231275541" style="display:none">I wanted to enjoy this, as I enjoyed Glen Duncan's "Last Werewolf" series. This has the same grittiness, salaciousness, and dirtiness, plus a dab of historic lore that adds some spice; but I just couldn't get into "I, Lucifer" as much.<br /><br />Glen Duncan's writing style is hard to follow at times, and the plot seems... I don't even know. It's sorta linear, but not really. Jumping back and forth between the Biblical times and Now, a time the Devil is loaned a human body by heavens to try things out. Body happens to be a writer, so Luce writes. But he can't just be a human doing human things, he has to do the most depraved things as well. The ol' "I'm the devil and it's what I do. You understand, yes?" <br /><br />The parts where we follow the Bible from Lucifer's perspective are probably the best parts of the story, for me. We actually do get, as the tagline suggests, his side of the story. But the present day storyline seems almost pointless and drawn out. A field day to show us just what the Devil would do in our time. And it's almost cliched, because it is terrible, and he's the devil... yes yes we know, get on with it, please. <br /><br />And in any case, a lot of it was rambling on and making me wish the chapters would end. And when it does end, it's rather abrupt. I didn't feel a sense of accomplishment or conclusion or purpose. Which, with a devil, is somewhat fitting, I guess? I wish I could give half stars, because it's somewhere between a 2 and 3 for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1535497269231275541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Robert Day" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13307338-robert-day"><img alt="Robert Day" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442972150p2/13307338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2086076942?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Day" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Day" href="/user/show/13307338-robert-day">Robert Day</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780743220132" href="/book/show/1293432.I_Lucifer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2086076942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9411530784007214447">Oscillated between four and three stars and them plumped for three because this promising book turned into something kinda profane and then ended with a whimper rather than the bang I wanted. Still, there's no accounting for other writer's tastes in finales.<br/><br/>Loved the parts where Satan enjoyed his month in the mortal realm. Tolerated the parts where he stepped out of character and considered staying mortal. Hated the parts where he ran his host body into the ground in search of sensory experience</span>
  <span id="freeText9411530784007214447" style="display:none">Oscillated between four and three stars and them plumped for three because this promising book turned into something kinda profane and then ended with a whimper rather than the bang I wanted. Still, there's no accounting for other writer's tastes in finales.<br /><br />Loved the parts where Satan enjoyed his month in the mortal realm. Tolerated the parts where he stepped out of character and considered staying mortal. Hated the parts where he ran his host body into the ground in search of sensory experience.<br /><br />I suppose it would have been even more out of character if Satan had actually intended to improve the lot of the host and the people around him, but I suppose it was enough that this happened inadvertently. God's doing I suppose.<br /><br />Learnt some stuff about the bible and about sin and about dogs. Learnt stuff about how the author thinks that life works.<br /><br />Interesting book. Would I warn myself not to read it if I had the ability to go back in time? Maybe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9411530784007214447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ySjq5/i9VFMxB3bdzF8rvQt0e3V1GMUf0zvsg+CKzOUPnxBn6Zt/K6lkHgxuF4XmWs7Vy134UiYMecpa7ClH/w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D0RnKb3CMmQGIUVztHWKsLX+zXL8Frxyxq+ouQUvqsnJ852prOQZHJ5CLaIWPSTr5ERjzNT2K0sZ7Y5gCYwh0w==')})
  }

When loyalties are tested, Handong is left questioning his secrets, his choices, and his very identity.\n\nBeijing Comrades is the story of a torrid love affair set against the sociopolitical unrest of late-eighties China. Due to its depiction of gay sexuality and its critique of the totalitarian government, it was originally published anonymously on an underground gay website within mainland China. This riveting and heartbreaking novel, circulated throughout China in 1998, quickly developed a cult following, and remains a central work of queer literature from the People\'s Republic of China. This is the first English-language translation of Beijing Comrades.\n\nBei Tong is the anonymous author of Beijing Comrades.       newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_2535386').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_2535386').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_2535386').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5210711222669967094">Aka <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8004236.Saul_Black' title='Saul Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Saul Black</a>.<br/><br/>Glen Duncan is a British author born in 1965 in Bolton, Lancashire, England to an Anglo-Indian family. He studied philosophy and literature at the universities of Lancaster and Exeter. In 1990 Duncan moved to London, where he worked as a bookseller for four years, writing in his spare time. In 1994 he visited India with his father (part roots odyssey, part research for a later work,</span>
  <span id="freeText5210711222669967094" style="display:none">Aka <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8004236.Saul_Black" title="Saul Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Saul Black</a>.<br /><br />Glen Duncan is a British author born in 1965 in Bolton, Lancashire, England to an Anglo-Indian family. He studied philosophy and literature at the universities of Lancaster and Exeter. In 1990 Duncan moved to London, where he worked as a bookseller for four years, writing in his spare time. In 1994 he visited India with his father (part roots odyssey, part research for a later work, The Bloodstone Papers) before continuing on to the United States, where he spent several months travelling the country by Amtrak train, writing much of what would become his first novel, Hope, published to critical acclaim on both sides of the Atlantic in 1997. Duncan lives in London. Recently, his 2002 novel I, Lucifer has had the film rights purchased, with actors such as Ewan Mcgregor, Jason Brescia, Jude Law, Vin Diesel, and Daniel Craig all being considered for roles in the forthcoming movie.<br /><br />(from Wikipedia)</span>
